<div id="review_1639970576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1639970576" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2240678-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399502299p2/2240678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1639970576?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/2240678-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782272151" href="/book/show/28186177-twenty-four-hours-in-the-life-of-a-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2240678-melissa?shelf=german-lit">german-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2240678-melissa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2240678-melissa?shelf=pushkin-press">pushkin-press</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1639970576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14386294251881012493">I received an ARC of this title from Pushkin via Netgalley.<br/><br/>Stefan Zweig is a master at writing short stories that are full of descriptive details, interesting characters and surprise plot twists. It is truly amazing that he manages to do this all within the span of 100 pages. The setting of this short piece is a hotel on the French Riviera where a group of upper class citizens from various countries are vacationing. A shocking social incident has occurred within their social circle and this scan</span>
  <span id="freeText14386294251881012493" style="display:none">I received an ARC of this title from Pushkin via Netgalley.<br /><br />Stefan Zweig is a master at writing short stories that are full of descriptive details, interesting characters and surprise plot twists. It is truly amazing that he manages to do this all within the span of 100 pages. The setting of this short piece is a hotel on the French Riviera where a group of upper class citizens from various countries are vacationing. A shocking social incident has occurred within their social circle and this scandal has all of the guests arguing and gossiping.<br /><br />The narrator, who never gives us his name, is staying on the Riveria and interacts with the other guests, incluing a German husband and wife, a “portly” Dane, an Italian married couple, and a distinguished and older English lady. This group of strangers usually just engage in small talk and mild jokes while eating their meals, but the disappearance of Madame Henriette has disturbed their peaceful routine. A young, handsome and garrulous Frenchman arrived at the hotel on the previous day and captivated everyone’s attention. Zweig shows his skill at describing characters with just the right mix of adjectives and metaphors:<br /><br />Indeed everything about him was soft, endearing, charming, but without any artifice or affectation. At a distance he might at first remind you slightly of those pink wax dummies to be seen adopting dandified poses in the window displays of large fashion stores, walking-stick in hand and representing the ideal of male beauty, but closer inspection dispelled any impression of foppishness, for—most unusually—his charm was natural and innate, and seemed an inseparable part of him.<br /><br />The shock comes when Madame Henriette, the wife of a wealthy businessman, disappears with the Frenchman after knowing him for only a couple of days. All of the guests at the hotel are very quick to condemn and judge Henriette for throwing away her marriage, her children and her reputation. The narrator is the only person who comes to Henriette’s defense and reminds the guests that it might have been possible that Henriette was caught in a “tedious, disappointing marriage” and thus had a valid reason for running off with a young man who was virtually a stranger. This heated debate has a profound effect on Mrs. C, the distinguished English lady, who requests a private meeting with the narrator.<br /><br />The story that Mrs. C. tells the narrator involves an incident in her life when she was forty-two, some twenty years earlier. The incident had left her so embarrassed and mortified that she never told a word of it to another soul, until now. Henriette’s impulsive decision to run away with the Frenchman has brought up old memories for Mrs. C. and she wants to unburden her soul from the guilt of her own folly. Mrs. C. tells the narrator that, as a widow who lost her husband to an unexpected illness, she traveled around Europe while grieving for her beloved spouse. Alone and miserable, she finds herself in Monte Carlo, one of her husband’s favorite places for entertainment, and meets a twenty-four-year old man with a serious gambling problem.<br /><br />The events that unfold between Mrs. C. and the gambler bring up feelings of passion, anger, redemption, impulsivity and regret. I don’t want to give away what happens between the widow and the young man, but I will say that Zweig has a gift for writing shocking and unexpected plot turns. I never would have guessed the ending to Mrs. C’s story and I was riveted until the very last page of this short book. Zweig shows us that he is an astute observer of human emotions; love, loneliness, passion and sexual desire can make us lose our minds and do irrational things which are completely out of character.<br /><br />One final aspect of Zweig’s writing that must be mentioned is his careful attention to detail, even in a short work like this novella. When Mrs. C. arrives at the casino, she describes the chiromancy—guessing a person’s moves by observing their hands— that her husband had taught her. This English woman spent hours observing the players’ hands which are much more telling than facial expression. Zweig writes about Mrs. C’s practice of chiromancy:<br /><br />All those pale, moving, waiting hands around the green table, all emerging from the ever-different caverns of the players’ sleeves, each a beast of prey ready to leap, each varying in shape and colour, some bare, others laden with rings and clinking bracelets, some hairy like wild beasts, some damp and writhing like eels, but all of them tense, vibrating with a vast impatience.<br /><br />Zweig’s description of the players via their hands is absolutely fascinating and absorbing and is another surprising gem found within the pages of this short piece.<br /><br />November is German Lit. Month hosted by Lizzy’s Literary Life and Beauty is a Sleeping Cat. The full list of reviews for this event can be found here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://germanlitmonth.blogspot.co.uk/">http://germanlitmonth.blogspot.co.uk/</a> and on Twitter #GermanLitMonth.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14386294251881012493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1639854238" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1639854238" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36555254-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536187488p2/36555254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1639854238?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/36555254-robin">Robin</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782272151" href="/book/show/28186177-twenty-four-hours-in-the-life-of-a-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1639854238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7129638200245121959">Originally written in 1927 and translated from original German, this novella is my first reading of Austrian born Zweig. I was delighted to be drawn into the story immediately, and intrigued all along the way. The writing is charming and captivating. It's a story about passion, impulsivity, loneliness, convention and guilt. An elderly woman tells the narrator the story of a 24 hour span in her life that took place many years prior, which has haunted and shaped the rest of her life. While the soc</span>
  <span id="freeText7129638200245121959" style="display:none">Originally written in 1927 and translated from original German, this novella is my first reading of Austrian born Zweig. I was delighted to be drawn into the story immediately, and intrigued all along the way. The writing is charming and captivating. It's a story about passion, impulsivity, loneliness, convention and guilt. An elderly woman tells the narrator the story of a 24 hour span in her life that took place many years prior, which has haunted and shaped the rest of her life. While the societal 'rules' are quite different now than they were in 1927 (which makes her actions much less shocking when looked through a modern lens), the emotions are very relatable. Many people still feel trapped by societal expectations and live their lives accordingly - these 24 hours represent a complete escape from those prison bars. I appreciated the lack of judgment toward the woman in the narrator's/author's voice. Well worth the hour or so it takes to read this gem!<br /><br /><i>I received a free copy of this book via Netgalley, in exchange for an honest review. Thank you, Pushkin Press! </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7129638200245121959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1aDLmzeOWLCPB4XYNnxeYa7uG6kE9YiTokfqz7BsF3ua0HaxOvaTMHIChmj15bMp889WfXyxCwzO8PgXIXm42A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JymYYnF1GP6sMdsZzLUJ921wf97JQqM2CXpldGwZ5LFoWSVIfA3TflE02KkPLOS/MFEyCrEGIKllzXes/QxLEg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25573.Stefan_Zweig">About Stefan Zweig</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25573.Stefan_Zweig"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1190140738p3/25573.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25573.Stefan_Zweig">Stefan Zweig
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
5,937
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16204265226792370058">Stefan Zweig was one of the world's most famous writers during the 1920s and 1930s, especially in the U.S., South America, and Europe. He produced novels, plays, biographies, and journalist pieces. Among his most famous works are <i>Beware of Pity</i>, <i>Letter from an Unknown Woman</i>, and <i>Mary, Queen of Scotland and the Isles</i>. He and his second wife committed suicide in 1942.<br/><br/>Zweig studied in Austria, France</span>
  <span id="freeText16204265226792370058" style="display:none">Stefan Zweig was one of the world's most famous writers during the 1920s and 1930s, especially in the U.S., South America, and Europe. He produced novels, plays, biographies, and journalist pieces. Among his most famous works are <i>Beware of Pity</i>, <i>Letter from an Unknown Woman</i>, and <i>Mary, Queen of Scotland and the Isles</i>. He and his second wife committed suicide in 1942.<br /><br />Zweig studied in Austria, France, and Germany before settling in Salzburg in 1913. In 1934, driven into exile by the Nazis, he emigrated to England and then, in 1940, to Brazil by way of New York. Finding only growing loneliness and disillusionment in their new surroundings, he and his second wife committed suicide.<br /><br />Zweig's interest in psychology and the teachings of Sigmund Freud led to his most characteristic work, the subtle portrayal of character. Zweig's essays include studies of Honoré de Balzac, Charles Dickens, and Fyodor Dostoyevsky (<i>Drei Meister</i>, 1920; <i>Three Masters</i>) and of Friedrich Hölderlin, Heinrich von Kleist, and Friedrich Nietzsche (<i>Der Kampf mit dem Dämon</i>, 1925; <i>Master Builders</i>). He achieved popularity with <i>Sternstunden der Menschheit</i> (1928; <i>The Tide of Fortune</i>), five historical portraits in miniature. He wrote full-scale, intuitive rather than objective, biographies of the French statesman Joseph Fouché (1929), Mary Stuart (1935), and others. His stories include those in <i>Verwirrung der Gefühle</i> (1925; <i>Conflicts</i>). He also wrote a psychological novel, <i>Ungeduld des Herzens</i> (1938; <i>Beware of Pity</i>), and translated works of Charles Baudelaire, Paul Verlaine, and Emile Verhaeren.<br /><br />Most recently, his works provided the inspiration for 2014 film <i>The Grand Budapest Hotel</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16204265226792370058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
